*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/combobox
    *   [Combobox](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/Combobox)
        
    *   [ComboboxDialog](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/ComboboxDialog)
        
    *   [ComboboxInput](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/ComboboxInput)
        
    *   [ComboboxPopup](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/ComboboxPopup)
        
    *   [ComboboxPopupContainer](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/ComboboxPopupContainer)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/Combobox#api)

----------------------------------------------------------

    `class [Combobox](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/Combobox) <V> {  protected textDirection: Signal<Direction>;  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly popup: Signal<[ComboboxPopup](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/ComboboxPopup) <V> | undefined>;  filterMode: InputSignal<"manual" | "auto-select" | "highlight">;  readonly disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly readonly: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly firstMatch: InputSignal<V | undefined>;  readonly expanded: Signal<any>;  readonly alwaysExpanded: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly inputElement: Signal<any>;  open(): void;  close(): void;}`
    
    

A signal wrapper for directionality.

A reference to the combobox element.

The combobox popup.

The filter mode for the combobox.

*   `manual`: The consumer is responsible for filtering the options.
*   `auto-select`: The combobox automatically selects the first matching option.
*   `highlight`: The combobox highlights matching text in the options without changing selection.

Whether the combobox is disabled.

Whether the combobox is read-only.

The value of the first matching item in the popup.

Whether the combobox is expanded.

Whether the combobox popup should always be expanded, regardless of user interaction.

Input element connected to the combobox, if any.

Opens the combobox to the selected item.

@returns`void`

Closes the combobox.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/combobox/Combobox#description)

--------------------------------------------------------------------------

The container element that wraps a combobox input and popup, and orchestrates its behavior.

The `ngCombobox` directive is the main entry point for creating a combobox and customizing its behavior. It coordinates the interactions between the `ngComboboxInput` and the popup, which is defined by a `ng-template` with the `ngComboboxPopupContainer` directive. If using the `CdkOverlay`, the `cdkConnectedOverlay` directive takes the place of `ngComboboxPopupContainer`.

    <div ngCombobox filterMode="highlight">  <input    ngComboboxInput    placeholder="Search for a state..."    [(value)]="searchString"  />  <ng-template ngComboboxPopupContainer>    <div ngListbox [(value)]="selectedValue">      @for (option of filteredOptions(); track option) {        <div ngOption [value]="option" [label]="option">          <span>{{option}}</span>        </div>      }    </div>  </ng-template></div>

Jump to details

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Option#api)

-------------------------------------------------------

    `class [Option](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Option) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  active: Signal<any>;  readonly @Input() id: InputSignal<any>;  protected searchTerm: Signal<string>;  @Input() value: InputSignal<V>;  @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  @Input() label: InputSignal<string | undefined>;  readonly selected: Signal<any>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Whether the option is currently active (focused).

A unique identifier for the option.

The text used by the typeahead search.

The value of the option.

Whether an item is disabled.

The text used by the typeahead search.

Whether the option is selected.

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Option#description)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------

A selectable option in an `ngListbox`.

This directive should be applied to an element (e.g., `<li>`, `<div>`) within an `ngListbox`. The `value` input is used to identify the option, and the `label` input provides the accessible name for the option.

    <li ngOption value="item-id" label="Item Name">  Item Name</li>

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuContent#api)

---------------------------------------------------------

    `class [MenuContent](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuContent)  {}`
    
    

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuContent#description)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------

Defers the rendering of the menu content.

This structural directive should be applied to an `ng-template` within a `ngMenu` or `ngMenuBar` to lazily render its content only when the menu is opened.

    <div ngMenu #myMenu="ngMenu">  <ng-template ngMenuContent>    <div ngMenuItem>Lazy Item 1</div>    <div ngMenuItem>Lazy Item 2</div>  </ng-template></div>

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCell#api)

------------------------------------------------------

    `class [GridCell](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCell)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly active: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly @Input() id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly @Input() role: InputSignal<"gridcell" | "columnheader" | "rowheader">;  readonly @Input() rowSpan: InputSignal<number>;  readonly @Input() colSpan: InputSignal<number>;  readonly @Input() rowIndex: InputSignal<number | undefined>;  readonly @Input() colIndex: InputSignal<number | undefined>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() @Output('selectedChange') selected: ModelSignal<boolean>;  readonly @Input() selectable: InputSignal<boolean>;  readonly @Input() orientation: InputSignal<"vertical" | "horizontal">;  readonly @Input() wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() tabindex: InputSignal<number | undefined>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Whether the cell is currently active (focused).

Text direction.

A unique identifier for the cell.

The ARIA role for the cell.

The number of rows the cell should span.

The number of columns the cell should span.

The index of this cell's row within the grid.

The index of this cell's column within the grid.

Whether the cell is disabled.

Whether the cell is selected.

Whether the cell is selectable.

Orientation of the widgets in the cell.

Whether widgets navigation wraps.

The tabindex override.

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCell#description)

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Represents a cell within a grid row. It is the primary focusable element within the grid. It can be disabled and can have its selection state managed through the `selected` input.

    <td ngGridCell [disabled]="isDisabled" [(selected)]="isSelected">  Cell Content</td>

    *   [Grid](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/Grid)
        
    *   [GridCell](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCell)
        
    *   [GridCellWidget](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCellWidget)
        
    *   [GridRow](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridRow)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/Grid#api)

--------------------------------------------------

    `class [Grid](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/Grid)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly @Input() enableSelection: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() focusMode: InputSignal<"roving" | "activedescendant">;  readonly @Input() rowWrap: InputSignal<"continuous" | "loop" | "nowrap">;  readonly @Input() colWrap: InputSignal<"continuous" | "loop" | "nowrap">;  readonly @Input() multi: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() selectionMode: InputSignal<"follow" | "explicit">;  readonly @Input() enableRangeSelection: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Text direction.

Whether selection is enabled for the grid.

Whether the grid is disabled.

Whether to allow disabled items to receive focus. When `true`, disabled items are focusable but not interactive. When `false`, disabled items are skipped during navigation.

The focus strategy used by the grid.

*   `roving`: Focus is moved to the active cell using `tabindex`.
*   `activedescendant`: Focus remains on the grid container, and `aria-activedescendant` is used to indicate the active cell.

The wrapping behavior for keyboard navigation along the row axis.

*   `continuous`: Navigation wraps from the last row to the first, and vice-versa.
*   `loop`: Navigation wraps within the current row.
*   `nowrap`: Navigation stops at the first/last item in the row.

The wrapping behavior for keyboard navigation along the column axis.

*   `continuous`: Navigation wraps from the last column to the first, and vice-versa.
*   `loop`: Navigation wraps within the current column.
*   `nowrap`: Navigation stops at the first/last item in the column.

Whether multiple cells in the grid can be selected.

The selection strategy used by the grid.

*   `follow`: The focused cell is automatically selected.
*   `explicit`: Cells are selected explicitly by the user (e.g., via click or spacebar).

Whether enable range selections (with modifier keys or dragging).

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/Grid#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------

The container for a grid. It provides keyboard navigation and focus management for the grid's rows and cells. It manages the overall behavior of the grid, including focus wrapping, selection, and disabled states.

    <table ngGrid [multi]="true" [enableSelection]="true">  @for (row of gridData; track row) {    <tr ngGridRow>      @for (cell of row; track cell) {        <td ngGridCell [disabled]="cell.disabled">          {{cell.value}}        </td>      }    </tr>  }</table>

Jump to details

---

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/listbox
    *   [Listbox](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Listbox)
        
    *   [Option](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Option)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Listbox#api)

--------------------------------------------------------

    `class [Listbox](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Listbox) <V> {  readonly id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly element: HTMLElement;  protected textDirection: Signal<Direction>;  protected items: Signal<OptionPattern<V>[]>;  orientation: InputSignal<"vertical" | "horizontal">;  multi: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  focusMode: InputSignal<"roving" | "activedescendant">;  selectionMode: InputSignal<"follow" | "explicit">;  typeaheadDelay: InputSignal<number>;  disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  values: ModelSignal<V[]>;  scrollActiveItemIntoView(options?: ScrollIntoViewOptions): void;  gotoFirst(): void;}`
    
    

A unique identifier for the listbox.

A reference to the host element.

A signal wrapper for directionality.

The Option UIPatterns of the child Options.

Whether the list is vertically or horizontally oriented.

Whether multiple items in the list can be selected at once.

Whether focus should wrap when navigating.

Whether to allow disabled items to receive focus. When `true`, disabled items are focusable but not interactive. When `false`, disabled items are skipped during navigation.

The focus strategy used by the list.

*   `roving`: Focus is moved to the active item using `tabindex`.
*   `activedescendant`: Focus remains on the listbox container, and `aria-activedescendant` is used to indicate the active item.

The selection strategy used by the list.

*   `follow`: The focused item is automatically selected.
*   `explicit`: Items are selected explicitly by the user (e.g., via click or spacebar).

The amount of time before the typeahead search is reset.

Whether the listbox is disabled.

Whether the listbox is readonly.

The values of the currently selected items.

@paramoptions`ScrollIntoViewOptions`

@returns`void`

Navigates to the first item in the listbox.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/listbox/Listbox#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Represents a container used to display a list of items for a user to select from.

The `ngListbox` is meant to be used in conjunction with `ngOption` directives to create a selectable list. It supports single and multiple selection modes, as well as various focus and orientation strategies.

    <ul ngListbox [(value)]="selectedItems" [multi]="true" orientation="vertical">  @for (item of items; track item.id) {    <li ngOption [value]="item.id" [label]="item.name" [disabled]="item.disabled">      {{item.name}}    </li>  }</ul>

Jump to details

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabContent#api)

--------------------------------------------------------

    `class [TabContent](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabContent)  {}`
    
    

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabContent#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------------

A TabContent container for the lazy-loaded content.

This structural directive should be applied to an `ng-template` within an `ngTabPanel`. It enables lazy loading of the tab's content, meaning the content is only rendered when the tab is activated for the first time.

    <div ngTabPanel value="myTabId">  <ng-template ngTabContent>    <p>This content will be loaded when 'myTabId' is selected.</p>  </ng-template></div>

Jump to details

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/menu
    *   [Menu](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu)
        
    *   [MenuBar](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuBar)
        
    *   [MenuContent](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuContent)
        
    *   [MenuItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuItem)
        
    *   [MenuTrigger](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuTrigger)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuBar#api)

-----------------------------------------------------

    `class [MenuBar](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuBar) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly @Input() @Output('valuesChange') values: ModelSignal<V[]>;  readonly @Input() wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() typeaheadDelay: InputSignal<number>;  @Output() onSelect: OutputEmitterRef<V>;  close(): void;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Whether the menubar is disabled.

Whether the menubar is soft disabled.

The directionality (LTR / RTL) context for the application (or a subtree of it).

The values of the currently selected menu items.

Whether the menu should wrap its items.

The delay in milliseconds before the typeahead buffer is cleared.

A callback function triggered when a menu item is selected.

Closes the menubar.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuBar#description)

---------------------------------------------------------------------

A menu bar of menu items.

Like the `ngMenu`, a `ngMenuBar` is used to offer a list of menu item choices to users. However, a menubar is used to display a persistent, top-level, always-visible set of menu item choices, typically found at the top of an application window.

    <div ngMenuBar>  <button ngMenuTrigger [menu]="fileMenu">File</button>  <button ngMenuTrigger [menu]="editMenu">Edit</button></div><div ngMenu #fileMenu="ngMenu">  <div ngMenuItem>New</div>  <div ngMenuItem>Open</div></div><div ngMenu #editMenu="ngMenu">  <div ngMenuItem>Cut</div>  <div ngMenuItem>Copy</div></div>

Jump to details

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/Tabs#api)

--------------------------------------------------

    `class [Tabs](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/Tabs)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/Tabs#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------

A Tabs container.

The `ngTabs` directive represents a set of layered sections of content. It acts as the overarching container for a tabbed interface, coordinating the behavior of `ngTabList`, `ngTab`, and `ngTabPanel` directives.

    <div ngTabs>  <ul ngTabList [(selectedTab)]="selectedTabValue">    <li ngTab value="tab1">Tab 1</li>    <li ngTab value="tab2">Tab 2</li>    <li ngTab value="tab3">Tab 3</li>  </ul>  <div ngTabPanel value="tab1">     <ng-template ngTabContent>Content for Tab 1</ng-template>  </div>  <div ngTabPanel value="tab2">     <ng-template ngTabContent>Content for Tab 2</ng-template>  </div>  <div ngTabPanel value="tab3">     <ng-template ngTabContent>Content for Tab 3</ng-template>  </div></div>

Jump to details

    *   [ToolbarWidgetGroup](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/ToolbarWidgetGroup)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/ToolbarWidget#api)

--------------------------------------------------------------

    `class [ToolbarWidget](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/ToolbarWidget) <V> implements [OnInit](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnInit)  ,[OnDestroy](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnDestroy)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly @Input() id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly hardDisabled: Signal<any>;  readonly @Input() value: InputSignal<V>;  readonly active: Signal<any>;  readonly selected: () => any;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

A unique identifier for the widget.

Whether the widget is disabled.

Whether the widget is 'hard' disabled, which is different from `aria-disabled`. A hard disabled widget cannot receive focus.

The value associated with the widget.

Whether the widget is currently active (focused).

Whether the widget is selected (only relevant in a selection group).

@returns`void`

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/ToolbarWidget#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------------------

A widget within a toolbar.

The `ngToolbarWidget` directive should be applied to any native HTML element that acts as an interactive widget within an `ngToolbar` or `ngToolbarWidgetGroup`. It enables keyboard navigation and selection within the toolbar.

    <button ngToolbarWidget value="action-id" [disabled]="isDisabled">  Perform Action</button>

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/toolbar
    *   [Toolbar](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/Toolbar)

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/Toolbar#api)

--------------------------------------------------------

    `class [Toolbar](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/Toolbar) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly @Input() orientation: InputSignal<"vertical" | "horizontal">;  @Input() softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() @Output('valuesChange') values: ModelSignal<V[]>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Text direction.

Whether the toolbar is vertically or horizontally oriented.

Whether to allow disabled items to receive focus. When `true`, disabled items are focusable but not interactive. When `false`, disabled items are skipped during navigation.

Whether the toolbar is disabled.

Whether focus should wrap when navigating.

The values of the selected widgets within the toolbar.

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/toolbar/Toolbar#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------------

A toolbar widget container for a group of interactive widgets, such as buttons or radio groups. It provides a single point of reference for keyboard navigation and focus management. It supports various orientations and disabled states.

    <div ngToolbar orientation="horizontal" [wrap]="true">  <button ngToolbarWidget value="save">Save</button>  <button ngToolbarWidget value="print">Print</button>  <div ngToolbarWidgetGroup [(value)]="selectedAlignment">    <button ngToolbarWidget value="left">Left</button>    <button ngToolbarWidget value="center">Center</button>    <button ngToolbarWidget value="right">Right</button>  </div></div>

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/grid
    *   [Grid](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/Grid)
        
    *   [GridCell](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCell)
        
    *   [GridCellWidget](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCellWidget)
        
    *   [GridRow](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridRow)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCellWidget#api)

------------------------------------------------------------

    `class [GridCellWidget](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCellWidget)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly active: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly @Input() id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly @Input() widgetType: InputSignal<"simple" | "complex" | "editable">;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() focusTarget: InputSignal<HTMLElement | [ElementRef](https://angular.dev/api/core/ElementRef) <any> | undefined>;  readonly @Output() onActivate: OutputEmitterRef<KeyboardEvent | FocusEvent | undefined>;  readonly @Output() onDeactivate: OutputEmitterRef<KeyboardEvent | FocusEvent | undefined>;  readonly @Input() tabindex: InputSignal<number | undefined>;  readonly isActivated: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <boolean>;  activate(): void;  deactivate(): void;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Whether the widget is currently active (focused).

A unique identifier for the widget.

The type of widget, which determines how it is activated.

Whether the widget is disabled.

The target that will receive focus instead of the widget.

Emits when the widget is activated.

Emits when the widget is deactivated.

The tabindex override.

Whether the widget is activated.

Activates the widget.

@returns`void`

Deactivates the widget.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCellWidget#description)

----------------------------------------------------------------------------

Represents an interactive element inside a [`GridCell`](https://angular.dev/api/aria/grid/GridCell)
. It allows for pausing grid navigation to interact with the widget.

When the user interacts with the widget (e.g., by typing in an input or opening a menu), grid navigation is temporarily suspended to allow the widget to handle keyboard events.

    <td ngGridCell>  <button ngGridCellWidget>Click Me</button></td>

Jump to details

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/tree
    *   [Tree](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/Tree)
        
    *   [TreeItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItem)
        
    *   [TreeItemGroup](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItemGroup)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/Tree#api)

--------------------------------------------------

    `class [Tree](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/Tree) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly orientation: InputSignal<"vertical" | "horizontal">;  readonly multi: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly selectionMode: InputSignal<"explicit" | "follow">;  readonly focusMode: InputSignal<"roving" | "activedescendant">;  readonly wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly typeaheadDelay: InputSignal<number>;  readonly values: ModelSignal<V[]>;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly nav: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly currentType: InputSignal<"page" | "step" | "location" | "date" | "time" | "true" | "false">;  scrollActiveItemIntoView(options?: ScrollIntoViewOptions): void;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

A unique identifier for the tree.

Orientation of the tree.

Whether multi-selection is allowed.

Whether the tree is disabled.

The selection strategy used by the tree.

*   `explicit`: Items are selected explicitly by the user (e.g., via click or spacebar).
*   `follow`: The focused item is automatically selected.

The focus strategy used by the tree.

*   `roving`: Focus is moved to the active item using `tabindex`.
*   `activedescendant`: Focus remains on the tree container, and `aria-activedescendant` is used to indicate the active item.

Whether navigation wraps.

Whether to allow disabled items to receive focus. When `true`, disabled items are focusable but not interactive. When `false`, disabled items are skipped during navigation.

The delay in seconds before the typeahead search is reset.

The values of the currently selected items.

Text direction.

The `aria-current` type. It can be used in navigation trees to indicate the currently active item. See [https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/Accessibility/ARIA/Reference/Attributes/aria-current](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/Accessibility/ARIA/Reference/Attributes/aria-current)
 for more details.

@paramoptions`ScrollIntoViewOptions`

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/Tree#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------

A container that transforms nested lists into an accessible, ARIA-compliant tree structure. It manages the overall state of the tree, including selection, expansion, and keyboard navigation.

    <ul ngTree [(value)]="selectedItems" [multi]="true">  <ng-template    [ngTemplateOutlet]="treeNodes"    [ngTemplateOutletContext]="{nodes: treeData, parent: tree}"  /></ul><ng-template #treeNodes let-nodes="nodes" let-parent="parent">  @for (node of nodes; track node.name) {    <li ngTreeItem [parent]="parent" [value]="node.name" [label]="node.name">      {{ node.name }}      @if (node.children) {        <ul role="group">          <ng-template ngTreeItemGroup [ownedBy]="treeItem" #group="ngTreeItemGroup">            <ng-template              [ngTemplateOutlet]="treeNodes"              [ngTemplateOutletContext]="{nodes: node.children, parent: group}"            />          </ng-template>        </ul>      }    </li>  }</ng-template>

Jump to details

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType#api)

--------------------------------------------------------------------

    `enum [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType)  {  State: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .State;  Transition: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Transition;  Sequence: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Sequence;  Group: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Group;  Animate: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Animate;  Keyframes: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Keyframes;  Style: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Style;  Trigger: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Trigger;  Reference: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Reference;  AnimateChild: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .AnimateChild;  AnimateRef: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .AnimateRef;  Query: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Query;  Stagger: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) .Stagger;}`
    
    

Associates a named animation state with a set of CSS styles. See [](https://angular.dev/api/animations/api/animations/state)
[`state()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/state)

Data for a transition from one animation state to another. See [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)

Contains a set of animation steps. See [`sequence()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)

Contains a set of animation steps. See `group()`

Contains an animation step. See [`animate()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animate)

Contains a set of animation steps. See [`keyframes()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/keyframes)

Contains a set of CSS property-value pairs into a named style. See [`style()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style)

Associates an animation with an entry trigger that can be attached to an element. See [`trigger()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/trigger)

Contains a re-usable animation. See [`animation()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animation)

Contains data to use in executing child animations returned by a query. See [`animateChild()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animateChild)

Contains animation parameters for a re-usable animation. See [`useAnimation()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)

Contains child-animation query data. See [`query()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/query)

Contains data for staggering an animation sequence. See [`stagger()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/stagger)

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Constants for the categories of parameters that can be defined for animations.

A corresponding function defines a set of parameters for each category, and collects them into a corresponding [`AnimationMetadata`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadata)
 object.

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/Tab#description)

-----------------------------------------------------------------

A selectable tab in a TabList.

The `ngTab` directive represents an individual tab control within an `ngTabList`. It requires a `value` that uniquely identifies it and links it to a corresponding `ngTabPanel`.

    <li ngTab value="myTabId" [disabled]="isTabDisabled">  My Tab Label</li>

------------------------------------------------------

    `class [TabPanel](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabPanel)  implements [OnInit](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnInit)  ,[OnDestroy](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnDestroy)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly value: InputSignal<string>;  readonly visible: Signal<boolean>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

A global unique identifier for the tab.

A local unique identifier for the tabpanel.

Whether the tab panel is visible.

@returns`void`

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabPanel#description)

----------------------------------------------------------------------

A TabPanel container for the resources of layered content associated with a tab.

The `ngTabPanel` directive holds the content for a specific tab. It is linked to an `ngTab` by a matching `value`. If a tab panel is hidden, the `inert` attribute will be applied to remove it from the accessibility tree. Proper styling is required for visual hiding.

    <div ngTabPanel value="myTabId">  <ng-template ngTabContent>    <!-- Content for the tab panel -->  </ng-template></div>

Jump to details

    *   @angular/localize/init

    *   @angular/platform-browser-dynamic
    *   @angular/platform-browser-dynamic/testing
    *   @angular/platform-browser/animations
    *   @angular/platform-browser/animations/async
    *   @angular/platform-browser/testing
    *   @angular/platform-server
    *   @angular/platform-server/testing
    *   @angular/router
    *   @angular/router/testing
    *   @angular/router/upgrade
    *   @angular/service-worker
    *   @angular/ssr
    *   @angular/ssr/node
    *   @angular/upgrade
    *   @angular/upgrade/static
    *   @angular/upgrade/static/testing
    *   window.ng globals

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/menu
    *   [Menu](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu)
        
    *   [MenuBar](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuBar)
        
    *   [MenuContent](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuContent)
        
    *   [MenuItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuItem)
        
    *   [MenuTrigger](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuTrigger)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu#api)

--------------------------------------------------

    `class [Menu](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly typeaheadDelay: InputSignal<number>;  readonly disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly parent: WritableSignal<[MenuTrigger](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuTrigger) <V> | [MenuItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuItem) <V> | undefined>;  readonly visible: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly tabIndex: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  onSelect: OutputEmitterRef<V>;  readonly expansionDelay: InputSignal<number>;  close(): void;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

The directionality (LTR / RTL) context for the application (or a subtree of it).

The unique ID of the menu.

Whether the menu should wrap its items.

The delay in milliseconds before the typeahead buffer is cleared.

Whether the menu is disabled.

A reference to the parent menu item or menu trigger.

Whether the menu is visible.

The tab index of the menu.

A callback function triggered when a menu item is selected.

The delay in milliseconds before expanding sub-menus on hover.

Closes the menu.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu#description)

------------------------------------------------------------------

A list of menu items.

A `ngMenu` is used to offer a list of menu item choices to users. Menus can be nested within other menus to create sub-menus. It works in conjunction with `ngMenuTrigger` and `ngMenuItem` directives.

    <button ngMenuTrigger [menu]="myMenu">Options</button><div ngMenu #myMenu="ngMenu">  <div ngMenuItem>Star</div>  <div ngMenuItem>Edit</div>  <div ngMenuItem [submenu]="subMenu">More</div></div><div ngMenu #subMenu="ngMenu">  <div ngMenuItem>Sub Item 1</div>  <div ngMenuItem>Sub Item 2</div></div>

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuItem#api)

------------------------------------------------------

    `class [MenuItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuItem) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly @Input() id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly @Input() value: InputSignal<V>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignal<boolean>;  readonly @Input() @Output('searchTermChange') searchTerm: ModelSignal<string>;  readonly parent: [Menu](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu) <V> | [MenuBar](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuBar) <V> | null;  readonly @Input() submenu: InputSignal<[Menu](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu) <V> | undefined>;  readonly active: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly expanded: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly hasPopup: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  open(): void;  close(): void;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

The unique ID of the menu item.

The value of the menu item.

Whether the menu item is disabled.

The search term associated with the menu item.

A reference to the parent menu or menubar.

The submenu associated with the menu item.

Whether the menu item is active.

Whether the menu is expanded.

Whether the menu item has a popup.

Opens the submenu focusing on the first menu item.

@returns`void`

Closes the submenu.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuItem#description)

----------------------------------------------------------------------

An item in a Menu.

`ngMenuItem` directives can be used in `ngMenu` and `ngMenuBar` to represent a choice or action a user can take. They can also act as triggers for sub-menus.

    <div ngMenuItem (onSelect)="doAction()">Action Item</div><div ngMenuItem [submenu]="anotherMenu">Submenu Trigger</div>

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuTrigger#api)

---------------------------------------------------------

    `class [MenuTrigger](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuTrigger) <V> {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  @Input() menu: InputSignal<[Menu](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/Menu) <V> | undefined>;  readonly expanded: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly hasPopup: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  open(): void;  close(): void;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

The directionality (LTR / RTL) context for the application (or a subtree of it).

The menu associated with the trigger.

Whether the menu is expanded.

Whether the menu trigger has a popup.

Whether the menu trigger is disabled.

Whether the menu trigger is soft disabled.

Opens the menu focusing on the first menu item.

@returns`void`

Closes the menu.

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/menu/MenuTrigger#description)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------

A trigger for a menu.

The `ngMenuTrigger` directive is used to open and close menus. It can be applied to any interactive element (e.g., a button) to associate it with a `ngMenu` instance. It also supports linking to sub-menus when applied to a `ngMenuItem`.

    <button ngMenuTrigger [menu]="myMenu">Open Menu</button><div ngMenu #myMenu="ngMenu">  <div ngMenuItem>Item 1</div>  <div ngMenuItem>Item 2</div></div>

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItem#api)

------------------------------------------------------

    `class [TreeItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItem) <V> extends DeferredContentAware implements [OnInit](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnInit)  ,[OnDestroy](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnDestroy)  ,HasElement {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly @Input() id: InputSignal<any>;  readonly @Input() value: InputSignal<V>;  readonly @Input() parent: InputSignal<[Tree](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/Tree) <V> | [TreeItemGroup](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItemGroup) <V>>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() selectable: InputSignal<boolean>;  readonly @Input() @Output('expandedChange') expanded: ModelSignal<boolean>;  readonly @Input() label: InputSignal<string | undefined>;  readonly searchTerm: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <string>;  readonly tree: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <[Tree](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/Tree) <V>>;  readonly active: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly level: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly selected: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;  readonly visible: [Signal](https://angular.dev/api/core/Signal) <any>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

A unique identifier for the tree item.

The value of the tree item.

The parent tree root or tree item group.

Whether the tree item is disabled.

Whether the tree item is selectable.

Whether the tree item is expanded.

Optional label for typeahead. Defaults to the element's textContent.

Search term for typeahead.

The tree root.

Whether the item is active.

The level of the current item in a tree.

Whether the item is selected.

Whether this item is visible due to all of its parents being expanded.

@returns`void`

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItem#description)

----------------------------------------------------------------------

A selectable and expandable item in an `ngTree`.

The `ngTreeItem` directive represents an individual node within an `ngTree`. It can be selected, expanded (if it has children), and disabled. The `parent` input establishes the hierarchical relationship within the tree.

    <li ngTreeItem [parent]="parentTreeOrGroup" value="item-id" label="Item Label">  Item Label</li>

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItemGroup#api)

-----------------------------------------------------------

    `class [TreeItemGroup](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItemGroup) <V> implements [OnInit](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnInit)  ,[OnDestroy](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnDestroy)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly ownedBy: InputSignal<[TreeItem](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItem) <V>>;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Tree item that owns the group.

@returns`void`

@returns`void`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tree/TreeItemGroup#description)

---------------------------------------------------------------------------

Group that contains children tree items.

The `ngTreeItemGroup` structural directive should be applied to an `ng-template` that wraps the child `ngTreeItem` elements. It is used to define a group of children for an expandable `ngTreeItem`. The `ownedBy` input links the group to its parent `ngTreeItem`.

    <li ngTreeItem [value]="'parent-id'">  Parent Item  <ul role="group">    <ng-template ngTreeItemGroup [ownedBy]="parentTreeItemRef">      <li ngTreeItem [value]="'child-id'">Child Item</li>    </ng-template>  </ul></li>

Jump to details

    *   [sequence](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)
        
    *   [stagger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/stagger)
        
    *   [state](https://angular.dev/api/animations/state)
        
    *   [style](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style)
        
    *   [transition](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
        
    *   [trigger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/trigger)
        
    *   [useAnimation](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
        

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions#api)

---------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [AnimationOptions](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions)  {  delay?: string | number | undefined;  params?: { [name: string]: any; } | undefined;}`
    
    

Sets a time-delay for initiating an animation action. A number and optional time unit, such as "1s" or "10ms" for one second and 10 milliseconds, respectively.The default unit is milliseconds. Default value is 0, meaning no delay.

A set of developer-defined parameters that modify styling and timing when an animation action starts. An array of key-value pairs, where the provided value is used as a default.

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions#description)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Options that control animation styling and timing.

The following animation functions accept [`AnimationOptions`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions)
 data:

*   [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
    
*   [`sequence()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)
    
*   `group()`
*   [`query()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/query)
    
*   [`animation()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animation)
    
*   [`useAnimation()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
    
*   [`animateChild()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animateChild)
    

Programmatic animations built using the [`AnimationBuilder`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationBuilder)
 service also make use of [`AnimationOptions`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions)
.

Jump to details

*   arrow\_back @angular/aria/tabs
    *   [Tab](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/Tab)
        
    *   [TabContent](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabContent)
        
    *   [TabList](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabList)
        
    *   [TabPanel](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabPanel)
        
    *   [Tabs](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/Tabs)
        

[API](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabList#api)

-----------------------------------------------------

    `class [TabList](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabList)  implements [OnInit](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnInit)  ,[OnDestroy](https://angular.dev/api/core/OnDestroy)  {  readonly element: HTMLElement;  readonly textDirection: WritableSignal<Direction>;  readonly @Input() orientation: InputSignal<"vertical" | "horizontal">;  readonly @Input() wrap: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() softDisabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  readonly @Input() focusMode: InputSignal<"roving" | "activedescendant">;  readonly @Input() selectionMode: InputSignal<"follow" | "explicit">;  readonly @Input() @Output('selectedTabChange') selectedTab: ModelSignal<string | undefined>;  readonly @Input() disabled: InputSignalWithTransform<boolean, unknown>;  open(value: string): boolean;}`
    
    

A reference to the host element.

Text direction.

Whether the tablist is vertically or horizontally oriented.

Whether focus should wrap when navigating.

Whether to allow disabled items to receive focus. When `true`, disabled items are focusable but not interactive. When `false`, disabled items are skipped during navigation.

The focus strategy used by the tablist.

*   `roving`: Focus is moved to the active tab using `tabindex`.
*   `activedescendant`: Focus remains on the tablist container, and `aria-activedescendant` is used to indicate the active tab.

The selection strategy used by the tablist.

*   `follow`: The focused tab is automatically selected.
*   `explicit`: Tabs are selected explicitly by the user (e.g., via click or spacebar).

The current selected tab.

Whether the tablist is disabled.

@returns`void`

@returns`void`

Opens the tab panel with the specified value.

@paramvalue`string`

@returns`boolean`

[Description](https://angular.dev/api/aria/tabs/TabList#description)

---------------------------------------------------------------------

A TabList container.

The `ngTabList` directive controls a list of `ngTab` elements. It manages keyboard navigation, selection, and the overall orientation of the tabs. It should be placed within an `ngTabs` container.

    <ul ngTabList [(selectedTab)]="mySelectedTab" orientation="horizontal" selectionMode="explicit">  <li ngTab value="first">First Tab</li>  <li ngTab value="second">Second Tab</li></ul>

Jump to details

One or more animation step objects.

An options object containing a delay and developer-defined parameters that provide styling defaults and can be overridden on invocation. Default delay is 0.

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationQueryOptions#api)

--------------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [AnimationQueryOptions](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationQueryOptions)  extends [AnimationOptions](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions)  {  optional?: boolean | undefined;  limit?: number | undefined;  override delay?: string | number | undefined;  override params?: { [name: string]: any; } | undefined;}`
    
    

True if this query is optional, false if it is required. Default is false. A required query throws an error if no elements are retrieved when the query is executed. An optional query does not.

A maximum total number of results to return from the query. If negative, results are limited from the end of the query list towards the beginning. By default, results are not limited.

Sets a time-delay for initiating an animation action. A number and optional time unit, such as "1s" or "10ms" for one second and 10 milliseconds, respectively.The default unit is milliseconds. Default value is 0, meaning no delay.

A set of developer-defined parameters that modify styling and timing when an animation action starts. An array of key-value pairs, where the provided value is used as a default.

Jump to details

---

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationPlayer#api)

--------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [AnimationPlayer](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationPlayer)  {  onDone(fn: () => void): void;  onStart(fn: () => void): void;  onDestroy(fn: () => void): void;  init(): void;  hasStarted(): boolean;  play(): void;  pause(): void;  restart(): void;  finish(): void;  destroy(): void;  reset(): void;  setPosition(position: number): void;  getPosition(): number;  parentPlayer: [AnimationPlayer](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationPlayer)  | null;  readonly totalTime: number;  beforeDestroy?: (() => any) | undefined;}`
    
    

Provides a callback to invoke when the animation finishes.

@paramfn`() => void`

The callback function.

@returns`void`

Provides a callback to invoke when the animation starts.

@paramfn`() => void`

The callback function.

@returns`void`

Provides a callback to invoke after the animation is destroyed.

@paramfn`() => void`

The callback function.

@returns`void`

Initializes the animation.

@returns`void`

Reports whether the animation has started.

@returns`boolean`

Runs the animation, invoking the `onStart()` callback.

@returns`void`

Pauses the animation.

@returns`void`

Restarts the paused animation.

@returns`void`

Ends the animation, invoking the `onDone()` callback.

@returns`void`

Destroys the animation, after invoking the `beforeDestroy()` callback. Calls the `onDestroy()` callback when destruction is completed.

@returns`void`

Resets the animation to its initial state.

@returns`void`

Sets the position of the animation.

@paramposition`number`

A fractional value, representing the progress through the animation.

@returns`void`

Reports the current position of the animation.

@returns`number`

The parent of this player, if any.

The total run time of the animation, in milliseconds.

Provides a callback to invoke before the animation is destroyed.

Jump to details

------------------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [AnimationSequenceMetadata](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationSequenceMetadata)  extends [AnimationMetadata](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadata)  {  steps: [AnimationMetadata](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadata) [];  options: [AnimationOptions](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationOptions)  | null;  override type: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) ;}`
    
    

An array of animation step objects.

An options object containing a delay and developer-defined parameters that provide styling defaults and can be overridden on invocation. Default delay is 0.

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationTriggerMetadata#api)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [AnimationTriggerMetadata](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationTriggerMetadata)  extends [AnimationMetadata](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadata)  {  name: string;  definitions: [AnimationMetadata](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadata) [];  options: { params?: { [name: string]: any; } | undefined; } | null;  override type: [AnimationMetadataType](https://angular.dev/api/animations/AnimationMetadataType) ;}`
    
    

The trigger name, used to associate it with an element. Unique within the component.

An animation definition object, containing an array of state and transition declarations.

An options object containing a delay and developer-defined parameters that provide styling defaults and can be overridden on invocation. Default delay is 0.

An expression that describes a state change.

One or more animation objects to which this transition applies.

An options object containing a delay and developer-defined parameters that provide styling defaults and can be overridden on invocation. Default delay is 0.

    *   [keyframes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/keyframes)
        
    *   [NoopAnimationPlayer](https://angular.dev/api/animations/NoopAnimationPlayer)
        
    *   [query](https://angular.dev/api/animations/query)
        
    *   [sequence](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)
        
    *   [stagger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/stagger)
        
    *   [state](https://angular.dev/api/animations/state)
        
    *   [style](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style)
        
    *   [transition](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
        
    *   [trigger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/trigger)
        
    *   [useAnimation](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
        

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animate#api)

------------------------------------------------------

    function animate(  timings: string | number,  styles?: AnimationStyleMetadata | AnimationKeyframesSequenceMetadata | null,): AnimationAnimateMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animate#usage-notes)

----------------------------------------------------------------------

Call within an animation [`sequence()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)
, [`group()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/group)
, or [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
 call to specify an animation step that applies given style data to the parent animation for a given amount of time.

### [Syntax Examples](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animate#syntax-examples)

**Timing examples**

The following examples show various `timings` specifications.

*   `animate(500)` : Duration is 500 milliseconds.
*   `animate("1s")` : Duration is 1000 milliseconds.
*   `animate("100ms 0.5s")` : Duration is 100 milliseconds, delay is 500 milliseconds.
*   `animate("5s ease-in")` : Duration is 5000 milliseconds, easing in.
*   `animate("5s 10ms cubic-bezier(.17,.67,.88,.1)")` : Duration is 5000 milliseconds, delay is 10 milliseconds, easing according to a bezier curve.

**Style examples**

The following example calls [`style()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style)
 to set a single CSS style.

    animate(500, style({ background: "red" }))

The following example calls [`keyframes()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/keyframes)
 to set a CSS style to different values for successive keyframes.

    animate(500, keyframes( [  style({ background: "blue" }),  style({ background: "red" }) ])

Jump to details

---

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animation#api)

--------------------------------------------------------

    function animation(  steps: AnimationMetadata | AnimationMetadata[],  options?: AnimationOptions | null,): AnimationReferenceMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animation#usage-notes)

------------------------------------------------------------------------

The following example defines a reusable animation, providing some default parameter values.

    var fadeAnimation = animation([  style({ opacity: '{{ start }}' }),  animate('{{ time }}',  style({ opacity: '{{ end }}'}))  ],  { params: { time: '1000ms', start: 0, end: 1 }});

The following invokes the defined animation with a call to [`useAnimation()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
, passing in override parameter values.

    useAnimation(fadeAnimation, {  params: {    time: '2s',    start: 1,    end: 0  }})

If any of the passed-in parameter values are missing from this call, the default values are used. If one or more parameter values are missing before a step is animated, [`useAnimation()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
 throws an error.

Jump to details

---

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animateChild#api)

-----------------------------------------------------------

    function animateChild(  options?: AnimateChildOptions | null,): AnimationAnimateChildMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animateChild#usage-notes)

---------------------------------------------------------------------------

Each time an animation is triggered in Angular, the parent animation has priority and any child animations are blocked. In order for a child animation to run, the parent animation must query each of the elements containing child animations, and run them using this function.

Note that this feature is designed to be used with [`query()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/query)
 and it will only work with animations that are assigned using the Angular animation library. CSS keyframes and transitions are not handled by this API.

Jump to details

---

### [Multiple Tokens](https://angular.dev/api/animations/query#multiple-tokens)

Tokens can be merged into a combined query selector string. For example:

     query(':self, .record:enter, .record:leave,

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/group#api)

----------------------------------------------------

    function group(  steps: AnimationMetadata[],  options?: AnimationOptions | null,): AnimationGroupMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/group#usage-notes)

--------------------------------------------------------------------

Grouped animations are useful when a series of styles must be animated at different starting times and closed off at different ending times.

When called within a [`sequence()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)
 or a [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
 call, does not continue to the next instruction until all of the inner animation steps have completed.

Jump to details

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence#api)

-------------------------------------------------------

    function sequence(  steps: AnimationMetadata[],  options?: AnimationOptions | null,): AnimationSequenceMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence#usage-notes)

-----------------------------------------------------------------------

When you pass an array of steps to a [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
 call, the steps run sequentially by default. Compare this to the [`group()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/group)
 call, which runs animation steps in parallel.

When a sequence is used within a [`group()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/group)
 or a [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
 call, execution continues to the next instruction only after each of the inner animation steps have completed.

Jump to details

---

    *   [trigger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/trigger)
        
    *   [useAnimation](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
        

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/keyframes#api)

--------------------------------------------------------

    function keyframes(  steps: AnimationStyleMetadata[],): AnimationKeyframesSequenceMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/keyframes#usage-notes)

------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use with the [`animate()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animate)
 call. Instead of applying animations from the current state to the destination state, keyframes describe how each style entry is applied and at what point within the animation arc. Compare [CSS Keyframe Animations](https://www.w3schools.com/css/css3_animations.asp)
.

### [Usage](https://angular.dev/api/animations/keyframes#usage)

In the following example, the offset values describe when each `backgroundColor` value is applied. The color is red at the start, and changes to blue when 20% of the total time has elapsed.

    // the provided offset valuesanimate("5s", keyframes([  style({ backgroundColor: "red", offset: 0 }),  style({ backgroundColor: "blue", offset: 0.2 }),  style({ backgroundColor: "orange", offset: 0.3 }),  style({ backgroundColor: "black", offset: 1 })]))

If there are no `offset` values specified in the style entries, the offsets are calculated automatically.

    animate("5s", keyframes([  style({ backgroundColor: "red" }) // offset = 0  style({ backgroundColor: "blue" }) // offset = 0.33  style({ backgroundColor: "orange" }) // offset = 0.66  style({ backgroundColor: "black" }) // offset = 1]))

Jump to details

---

[API](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironment#api)

---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

    `class [ProtractorHarnessEnvironment](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironment)  extends HarnessEnvironment<ElementFinder> {  protected constructor(rawRootElement: ElementFinder, options?: [ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined): [ProtractorHarnessEnvironment](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironment) ;  forceStabilize(): Promise<void>;  protected getDocumentRoot(): ElementFinder;  protected createTestElement(element: ElementFinder): TestElement;  protected createEnvironment(element: ElementFinder): HarnessEnvironment<ElementFinder>;  protected getAllRawElements(selector: string): Promise<ElementFinder[]>;  static loader(options?: [ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined): HarnessLoader;  static getNativeElement(el: TestElement): ElementFinder;}`
    
    

@paramrawRootElement`ElementFinder`

@paramoptions`[ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined`

@returns`[ProtractorHarnessEnvironment](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironment) `

Flushes change detection and async tasks captured in the Angular zone. In most cases it should not be necessary to call this manually. However, there may be some edge cases where it is needed to fully flush animation events.

@returns`Promise<void>`

Gets the root element for the document.

@returns`ElementFinder`

Creates a `TestElement` from a raw element.

@paramelement`ElementFinder`

@returns`TestElement`

Creates a `HarnessLoader` rooted at the given raw element.

@paramelement`ElementFinder`

@returns`HarnessEnvironment<ElementFinder>`

Gets a list of all elements matching the given selector under this environment's root element.

@paramselector`string`

@returns`Promise<ElementFinder[]>`

Creates a `HarnessLoader` rooted at the document root.

@paramoptions`[ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/protractor/ProtractorHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined`

@returns`HarnessLoader`

Gets the ElementFinder corresponding to the given TestElement.

@paramel`TestElement`

@returns`ElementFinder`

    *   [query](https://angular.dev/api/animations/query)
        
    *   [sequence](https://angular.dev/api/animations/sequence)
        
    *   [stagger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/stagger)
        
    *   [state](https://angular.dev/api/animations/state)
        
    *   [style](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style)
        
    *   [transition](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
        
    *   [trigger](https://angular.dev/api/animations/trigger)
        
    *   [useAnimation](https://angular.dev/api/animations/useAnimation)
        

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/state#api)

----------------------------------------------------

    function state(  name: string,  styles: AnimationStyleMetadata,  options?: { params: { [name: string]: any } } | undefined,): AnimationStateMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/state#usage-notes)

--------------------------------------------------------------------

Use the [`trigger()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/trigger)
 function to register states to an animation trigger. Use the [`transition()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition)
 function to animate between states. When a state is active within a component, its associated styles persist on the element, even when the animation ends.

Jump to details

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/stagger#api)

------------------------------------------------------

    function stagger(  timings: string | number,  animation: AnimationMetadata | AnimationMetadata[],): AnimationStaggerMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/stagger#usage-notes)

----------------------------------------------------------------------

In the following example, a container element wraps a list of items stamped out by an `@for` block. The container element contains an animation trigger that will later be set to query for each of the inner items.

Each time items are added, the opacity fade-in animation runs, and each removed item is faded out. When either of these animations occur, the stagger effect is applied after each item's animation is started.

    <!-- list.component.html --><button (click)="toggle()">Show / Hide Items</button><hr /><div [@listAnimation]="items.length">  @for(item of items; track $index) {     <div>{{ item }}</div>  }</div>

Here is the component code:

    import {trigger, transition, style, animate, query, stagger} from '@angular/animations';@Component({  templateUrl: 'list.component.html',  animations: [    trigger('listAnimation', [    ...    ])  ]})class ListComponent {  items = [];  showItems() {    this.items = [0,1,2,3,4];  }  hideItems() {    this.items = [];  }  toggle() {    this.items.length ? this.hideItems() : this.showItems();   } }

Here is the animation trigger code:

    trigger('listAnimation', [  transition('* => *', [ // each time the binding value changes    query(':leave', [      stagger(100, [        animate('0.5s', style({ opacity: 0 }))      ])    ]),    query(':enter', [      style({ opacity: 0 }),      stagger(100, [        animate('0.5s', style({ opacity: 1 }))      ])    ])  ])])

Jump to details

---

@paramrawRootElement`Element`

@param\_fixture`[ComponentFixture](https://angular.dev/api/core/testing/ComponentFixture) <unknown>`

@paramoptions`[TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/testbed/TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined`

@returns`[TestbedHarnessEnvironment](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/testbed/TestbedHarnessEnvironment) `

Flushes change detection and async tasks captured in the Angular zone. In most cases it should not be necessary to call this manually. However, there may be some edge cases where it is needed to fully flush animation events.

@returns`Promise<void>`

Waits for all scheduled or running async tasks to complete. This allows harness authors to wait for async tasks outside of the Angular zone.

This only works when Zone.js is present _and_ patches are applied to the test framework by `zone.js/testing` (Jasmine and Jest only) or another script.

@returns`Promise<void>`

Gets the root element for the document.

@returns`Element`

Creates a `TestElement` from a raw element.

@paramelement`Element`

@returns`TestElement`

Creates a `HarnessLoader` rooted at the given raw element.

@paramelement`Element`

@returns`HarnessEnvironment<Element>`

Gets a list of all elements matching the given selector under this environment's root element.

@paramselector`string`

@returns`Promise<Element[]>`

Creates a `HarnessLoader` rooted at the given fixture's root element.

@paramfixture`[ComponentFixture](https://angular.dev/api/core/testing/ComponentFixture) <unknown>`

@paramoptions`[TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/testbed/TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined`

@returns`HarnessLoader`

Creates a `HarnessLoader` at the document root. This can be used if harnesses are located outside of a fixture (e.g. overlays appended to the document body).

@paramfixture`[ComponentFixture](https://angular.dev/api/core/testing/ComponentFixture) <unknown>`

@paramoptions`[TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/testbed/TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined`

@returns`HarnessLoader`

Gets the native DOM element corresponding to the given TestElement.

@paramel`TestElement`

@returns`Element`

Creates an instance of the given harness type, using the fixture's root element as the harness's host element. This method should be used when creating a harness for the root element of a fixture, as components do not have the correct selector when they are created as the root of the fixture.

@paramfixture`[ComponentFixture](https://angular.dev/api/core/testing/ComponentFixture) <unknown>`

@paramharnessType`ComponentHarnessConstructor<T>`

@paramoptions`[TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/testbed/TestbedHarnessEnvironmentOptions)  | undefined`

@returns`Promise<T>`

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style#api)

----------------------------------------------------

    function style(  tokens:    | '*'    | { [key: string]: string | number }    | ('*' | { [key: string]: string | number })[],): AnimationStyleMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/style#usage-notes)

--------------------------------------------------------------------

The following examples create animation styles that collect a set of CSS property values:

    // string values for CSS propertiesstyle({ background: "red", color: "blue" })// numerical pixel valuesstyle({ width: 100, height: 0 })

The following example uses auto-styling to allow an element to animate from a height of 0 up to its full height:

    style({ height: 0 }),animate("1s", style({ height: "*" }))

Jump to details

@returns`Promise<void>`

Click the element at the default location for the current environment. If you need to guarantee the element is clicked at a specific location, consider using `click('center')` or `click(x, y)` instead.

@returns`Promise<void>`

@paramrelativeY`number`

Coordinate within the element, along the Y-axis at which to click.

Modifier keys held while clicking

@returns`Promise<void>`

[API](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/AutoChangeDetectionStatus#api)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [AutoChangeDetectionStatus](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/AutoChangeDetectionStatus)  {  isDisabled: boolean;  onDetectChangesNow?: (() => void) | undefined;}`
    
    

Whether auto change detection is disabled.

An optional callback, if present it indicates that change detection should be run immediately, while handling the status change. The callback should then be called as soon as change detection is done.

Deprecation warning

Use `animate.enter` or `animate.leave` instead. Intent to remove in v23

[API](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition#api)

---------------------------------------------------------

    function transition(  stateChangeExpr:    | string    | ((        fromState: string,        toState: string,        element?: any,        params?: { [key: string]: any } | undefined,      ) => boolean),  steps: AnimationMetadata | AnimationMetadata[],  options?: AnimationOptions | null,): AnimationTransitionMetadata;

[Usage Notes](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition#usage-notes)

-------------------------------------------------------------------------

### [State Change Expression](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition#state-change-expression)

The State Change Expression instructs Angular when to run the transition's animations, it can either be

*   a string with a specific syntax
*   or a function that compares the previous and current state (value of the expression bound to the element's trigger) and returns `true` if the transition should occur or `false` otherwise

The string format can be:

*   `fromState => toState`, which indicates that the transition's animations should occur then the expression bound to the trigger's element goes from `fromState` to `toState`
    
    _Example:_
    
            transition('open => closed', animate('.5s ease-out', style({ height: 0 }) ))
    
*   `fromState <=> toState`, which indicates that the transition's animations should occur then the expression bound to the trigger's element goes from `fromState` to `toState` or vice versa
    
    _Example:_
    
            transition('enabled <=> disabled', animate('1s cubic-bezier(0.8,0.3,0,1)'))
    
*   `:enter`/`:leave`, which indicates that the transition's animations should occur when the element enters or exists the DOM
    
    _Example:_
    
            transition(':enter', [      style({ opacity: 0 }),      animate('500ms', style({ opacity: 1 }))    ])
    
*   `:increment`/`:decrement`, which indicates that the transition's animations should occur when the numerical expression bound to the trigger's element has increased in value or decreased
    
    _Example:_
    
            transition(':increment', query('@counter', animateChild()))
    
*   a sequence of any of the above divided by commas, which indicates that transition's animations should occur whenever one of the state change expressions matches
    
    _Example:_
    
            transition(':increment, * => enabled, :enter', animate('1s ease', keyframes([      style({ transform: 'scale(1)', offset: 0}),      style({ transform: 'scale(1.1)', offset: 0.7}),      style({ transform: 'scale(1)', offset: 1})    ]))),
    

Also note that in such context:

*   `void` can be used to indicate the absence of the element
*   asterisks can be used as wildcards that match any state
*   (as a consequence of the above, `void => *` is equivalent to `:enter` and `* => void` is equivalent to `:leave`)
*   `true` and `false` also match expression values of `1` and `0` respectively (but do not match _truthy_ and _falsy_ values)

Be careful about entering end leaving elements as their transitions present a common pitfall for developers.

Note that when an element with a trigger enters the DOM its `:enter` transition always gets executed, but its `:leave` transition will not be executed if the element is removed alongside its parent (as it will be removed "without warning" before its transition has a chance to be executed, the only way that such transition can occur is if the element is exiting the DOM on its own).

### [Animating to a Final State](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition#animating-to-a-final-state)

If the final step in a transition is a call to [`animate()`](https://angular.dev/api/animations/animate)
 that uses a timing value with no `style` data, that step is automatically considered the final animation arc, for the element to reach the final state, in such case Angular automatically adds or removes CSS styles to ensure that the element is in the correct final state.

### [Usage Examples](https://angular.dev/api/animations/transition#usage-examples)

*   Transition animations applied based on the trigger's expression value

      <div [@myAnimationTrigger]="myStatusExp">   ...  </div>

      trigger("myAnimationTrigger", [    ..., // states    transition("on => off, open => closed", animate(500)),    transition("* <=> error", query('.indicator', animateChild()))  ])

*   Transition animations applied based on custom logic dependent on the trigger's expression value and provided parameters
    
        <div [@myAnimationTrigger]="{ value: stepName, params: { target: currentTarget }}"> ...</div>
    
        trigger("myAnimationTrigger", [  ..., // states  transition(    (fromState, toState, _element, params) =>      ['firststep', 'laststep'].includes(fromState.toLowerCase())      && toState === params?.['target'],    animate('1s')  )])
    

Jump to details

[API](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/ComponentHarnessConstructor#api)

---------------------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [ComponentHarnessConstructor](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/ComponentHarnessConstructor) <T extends [ComponentHarness](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/ComponentHarness) > {  hostSelector: string;}`
    
    

[`ComponentHarness`](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/ComponentHarness)
 subclasses must specify a static `hostSelector` property that is used to find the host element for the corresponding component. This property should match the selector for the Angular component.

------------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [BaseHarnessFilters](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/BaseHarnessFilters)  {  selector?: string | undefined;  ancestor?: string | undefined;}`
    
    

Only find instances whose host element matches the given selector.

Only find instances that are nested under an element with the given selector.

-----------------------------------------------------------------

    `interface [ElementDimensions](https://angular.dev/api/cdk/testing/ElementDimensions)  {  top: number;  left: number;  width: number;  height: number;}`
    
    

The distance from the top of the viewport in pixels

The distance from the left of the viewport in pixels

The width of the element in pixels

The height of the element in pixels
